I'm having some troubles getting Xitami 'watertight'.

There is a little thing I have found out. Xitami is returning 2
different errors when trying to get files from areas where the user
shouldn't have access to.

When the file exists, it returns:
    403 forbidden

When it doesn't exist, it returns:
    404 not found

It would be better if it just returned '403 forbidden', else I could
write a program to find out which files there are on the server.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Nov  1 20:27:38 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Simon McVittie)
Date: Thu, 01 Nov 2001 20:27:38 +0000
Subject: [Xitami] memtrace
In-Reply-To: Your message of "Thu, 01 Nov 2001 13:14:19 +0100."
 <5.1.0.14.2.20011101131309.00abb738@pop.gmx.at>
References: <5.1.0.14.2.20011101131309.00abb738@pop.gmx.at>
Message-ID: <E15zOR8-0001vH-00@entropy.ucam.org>

Looking at the source code, it seems to be a debug file the iMatix Standard 
Function Library generates while exiting if it discovers a memory leak (the 
programmers at iMatix are very careful about memory leaks, which is 
probably why Xitami takes up so little memory... many programs leak memory 
quite badly, which is why you need to restart them and/or Windows so often).

It should never be generated; the fact that it has means something broke. 
I'm sure it shouldn't be as large as 8GB though... how long had Xitami been 
running for?

I'm not sure how to avoid it. Creating a read-only file called memtrace.lst 
might possibly block Xitami from writing it (the name is hard-coded, it 
won't try other names like it does with the logfiles).

to iMatix programmers
=====================

Should mem_assert even be enabled in a production build? sflmem.h seems to 
define it even when DEBUG isn't #defined - shouldn't it be an abort or even 
a no-op outside debug mode, rather than generating a huge log before it 
aborts?
It appears it's only called just before exit, anyway.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Nov  1 23:44:15 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Simon McVittie)
Date: Thu, 01 Nov 2001 23:44:15 +0000
Subject: [Xitami] memtrace

 <5.1.0.14.2.20011101214531.00ad5360@pop.chello.at>
References: <5.1.0.14.2.20011101131309.00abb738@pop.gmx.at>
 <5.1.0.14.2.20011101214531.00ad5360@pop.chello.at>
Message-ID: <E15zRVP-0002Os-00@entropy.ucam.org>

> >It should never be generated; the fact that it has means something broke.
> >I'm sure it shouldn't be as large as 8GB though... how long had Xitami been
> >running for?
> 
> 
> In fact, only 5 hours. Hard to believe such a writing rate.

>From more source code reading, it's actually all written on exit, but the file is a record of *all* the memory Xitami allocated and deallocated (which will probably only be a few bytes at a time in some places). 8GB in 5 hours does seem about right for that, but writing the file at all seems like debug-version behaviour.

Try creating a read-only file with the same name in the same folder... if this problem persists and Xitami manages to overwrite it, you'll just have to clean up after it when you exit :-( You could also try a different Xitami version and see if whatever memory leak caused this has been fixed.


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Nov  2 00:26:54 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 02 Nov 2001 13:26:54 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] memtrace
In-Reply-To: Message from "Simon McVittie" <sjm212@hermes.cam.ac.uk>
 of "Thu, 01 Nov 2001 23:44:15 -0000." <E15zRVP-0002Os-00@entropy.ucam.org>
Message-ID: <200111020026.NAA25978@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <E15zRVP-0002Os-00@entropy.ucam.org>, "Simon McVittie" writes:
>> >It should never be generated; the fact that it has means something broke.
>> >I'm sure it shouldn't be as large as 8GB though... how long had Xitami been
>> >running for?
>> 
>> In fact, only 5 hours. Hard to believe such a writing rate.
>
>From more source code reading, it's actually all written on exit, but the file
>is a record of *all* the memory Xitami allocated and deallocated (which will 
>probably only be a few bytes at a time in some places). 

The file is written on exit, if there is any memory that was allocated
but has not been freed.  It lists only the memory that was allocated,
but not freed, including where it was allocated.

To have written an 8GB file, the pointers through the memory allocated
must have got themselves into a nasty loop somewhere, so you'll probably
find the 8GB file contains a _lot_ of repeats.

As to whether it should be enabled in a production version; that's a
matter for opinion.  We generally try for "zero leaks" (because that's a
whole lot better if you're leaving something running for a long time),
and thus in theory it shouldn't matter if it's enabled in a production
version.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

it works and shows env. variables.

opening this pg.

>Does Xitami support SSI????

Yes.  With the help of a perl script in the case of the (production) 2.4
release, and internally in the case of the (beta) 2.5.

NOTE that this is the "core" SSI support, not various extensions that
some webservers have added on.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Nov  2 16:25:33 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Hugo Notti)
Date: Fri, 02 Nov 2001 17:25:33 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] simple cgi question
In-Reply-To: <200111021353.FAA29026@eskimo.com>
References: <"goldtech@worldpost.com" <goldtech@worldpost.com>
Message-ID: <5.1.0.14.2.20011102172129.00a47cc0@pop.gmx.net>

Check the following:

*.pl does not need to be bound to perl.exe
the path is irrelevant.
perl.exe must be in the path-statement of your computer so Xitami is able 
to find it.
if your script is called hello, it should work then.
if it is called hello.pl you need to call hello.pl of course (not even 
windows ignores the file endings, it just does not show them by default).
it is possible that you have to call the script from a html-page inside xitami.
if all of the above does not work, you should check your installation and 
maybe even check if you have saved the script as plain text or not.

Good luck,

Hugo

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Nov  3 06:07:34 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Patrick Olson)
Date: Fri, 02 Nov 2001 23:07:34 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Server Side Includes
References: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCGEPECDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <3BE389A6.1E121C82@qwest.net>

"Alvaro E. Siman" wrote:
> 
> How do I get to this archive.  Please respond with the URL.  All I have

This is how I got Perl running in Xitami
it allows me to use,

<!--#exec cgi="/cgi-bin/test.pl" -->

This SSI command
which is a potential security risk for your system
is only accepted if the environment variable
SSI_INSECURE is set to 'yes'
Under Windows NT
in the System Control Panel
under 'Environment
-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
Start->Settings->Control Panel
 
Double click on System
 
>From the pop-up box select the Environment tab
 
 In the Variable entry field type SSI_INSECURE
 In the Value entry field type YES
 (Make sure it goes where you want it,
  System Variables probably.)
 
Click OK
 
Reboot?  (I don't know if this is required.)
-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

under Windows 95/98 by adding
SET SSI_INSECURE=yes to the autoexec.bat. 
to run SSI.
If Perl is installed correctly?
On a windows system,
You then should be able to call
Perl from anywhere in your system.
This allows the shebang to be #! perl -w
and does not need to be like this
#! c:\perl\bin\perl.exe
this also allows the use of
#! /usr/bin/perl
for the shebang. so as long
as we don't use win32 specific modules
or system calls we can keep our programs
cross platform Compatible.

Running Windows98
Xitami v2.4d6

in your
autoexec.bat

SET PATH=C:\PERL\BIN;%PATH%
SET SSI_INSECURE=YES

defaults.cfg
[Filter]
    .shtm=perlssi
    .shtml=perlssi 
    .ssi=perlssi   
[Ssi]
    Enabled=1
    Exec=1

hope this helps
http://127.0.0.1/xitami/index5.htm
http://127.0.0.1/xitami/index6.htm

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Nov  3 13:06:11 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (David Lambert)

Subject: [Xitami] CGI Scripting
In-Reply-To: <000301c15e29$a7e24ae0$6400000a@techapp.co.uk>
Message-ID: <000001c16468$503b3b40$6400000a@techapp.co.uk>

Thanks you all for the replies, including those concerning the disclaimer.
It's part and parcel of living in the UK now, where privacy laws are under
considerable threat. Our govt. likes to snoop, so does your but they haven't
told you yet!

Anyway, I digress. It turns out that all I needed to do was to add the
following to read the working directory of the initiating script i.e.
		$DocRoot = $ENV{'DOCUMENT_ROOT'};

Then by appending this to the 'open(script)' command it worked OK.


Please forgive the coding samples, I only started on Perl a couple of weeks
ago. Lots to learn still... but such a powerful language.

Regards & Thanks

David

-----Original Message-----
From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
[mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org]On Behalf Of David Lambert
Sent: 26 October 2001 15:23
To: dlamb@tech-app.co.uk
Subject: [Xitami] CGI Scripting


I have a Perl script in webroot/cgi-bin, which reads a text file in and
outputs it in HTML format to the requesting browser (see smaple script
below). Well, that's what it's supposed to do.

It works at the DOS prompt, opening the file and printing output to the
screen. However, if I try the script through a browser, the server returns
no file contents. I assumed the problem was a permissions error, so as a
brute force resolution, I gave Everyone, Full Permissions to the cgi-bin
directory, which still doesn't work.

The Xitami server itself is running under the NT Administrator user, so
should definitely be included in the Everyone group and have full
permissions to all files on the local machine. The working dir. is set to
"-" as recommended, yet it manages to create temporary files in D:\Temp,
which contain the output sent to the screen. So why can't it read in the
files?
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Sample Script:

#!perl

# Define Variables
	$Script;
	$lines;

# Read Name of Script
	$Script = $ENV{'SCRIPT_NAME'};
	if ($Script eq "") {$Script = "default.txt"};

# Open Script
	open(TXT, "<".$Script);
	@text=<TXT>;
	close(TXT);

# Print Script to screen
	&Header;
	print "\nScript to be processed: <b>".$Script."</b><hr>";
	foreach $line(@text){
		print "$line.<br>";
		$lines++;
	}
	if($lines<1){$lines="no"};
	&Footer;

sub Header{
	print "content-type:text/html\n\n<html>";
	print "<title>View File Script</title>";
}

sub Footer{
	print "There are <b>".$lines."</b> lines<br>";
	print "<b>The End</b>";
	print "</html>";
}
#	End viewfile.pl

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Nov  4 21:03:06 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Carl J. Elitz)
Date: Sun, 4 Nov 2001 15:03:06 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] FTP server woes...
Message-ID: <AIEJLJENNEEGIDEIELPGMEHDCAAA.reds@chicagonet.net>

I have installed Xitami and the web server works well. However, I cannot get
FTP to work, which is most frustrating. I suspect my setup is a bit
unusual... can anyone help?

I have an ISDN connection and my machine is behind a router which does NAT.
Because I have a dynamic IP address, I use TZO.com. (I have registered my
domain name to TZO's name servers; software on my machine monitors my
changing IP address and passes this info to TZO, which redirects traffic
which hits its servers looking for me back to my machine.)

People hitting my FTP server typically just get the time-out message.
Occassionally, someone gets logged on anonymously, but then the system drops
them when they try to download something. A tech at TZO was able to upload a
file to my machine, but not download. On my side of the router, everything
seems to work perfectly (the machines that I have can use the FTP service -
although only by using the local machine numbers as addresses... they are
not able to use my internet domain name, something I understand is normal
for being behind a router.)

I noticed that there is a setting in Xitami for Dynamic DNS. I have not been
able to get this configured properly, and suspect this could be the
problem's cause, although I am not even sure of this.

Here is the details on the DDNS settings:

1. Enable DNS sign on? YES/NO (default is NO)
2. DDNS service definition file:  (default is "ddnsdef.xml")
3. Dynamic DNS service:  Default is "DDNS test using localhost".
4. Your server domain name: (no default).
5. Your username or e-mail adddress: (no default). I have given my email
address, which is the user name used by TZO.com.
6. Your password or DDNS key: (no default). I have supplied the TZO "key"
which TZO assigned to me.

I have tried setting No. 1 to YES, No. 2 to the default file of
"ddnsdef.xml", No. 3. to "TZO.com", No. 4 to "elitz.com" and also tried the
name of my local machine, No. 5 to
"reds@chicagonet.net" (my email address), and No. 6 to my assigned TZO key
for elitz.com.

The ddnsdef.xml file has a section relevant to when No. 3 is set to
"TZO.com".  It reads as follows:

<!-----------------------------------------------------------------------
    tzo.com

    Service for tzo.com domains.  TZO uses an e-mail address as the
username,
    and a generated key as password.  Fast DNS updates.
    --------------------------------------------------------------------->
<SERVICE
  NAME  = "tzo.com"
  TITLE = "tzo.com"
  HOST  = "rh.tzo.com"
  URL   = "tzo.com"
  PORT  = "21333" >
  <SIGNON
    URL  = "/webclient/rhsignedon.html"
    ARGS =
"TZOName=$(domain)&Email=$(username)&TZOKey=$(password)&CType=6&B1=Sign+On+t
o+TZO+DDNS+Servers"
    SEND = "GET $(url)?$(args) HTTP/1.0\r\n$(httpheaders)" />
  <SIGNOFF
    URL  = "/webclient/signedoff.html"
    ARGS = "B1=Sign+Me+Off+from+TZO"
    SEND = "GET $(url)?$(args) HTTP/1.0\r\n$(httpheaders)" />
</SERVICE>

-----------------------------------------------------------------------

The error message generated in the Xitami console message window is:

2001/11/04 14:53:21: xiddns: 'localhost': HTTP/1.1 404 Not found

The TZO tech has asked that I work with Xitami people, as he is not sure of
the problem. He seemed to feel that the problem was that Xitami is using IP
references that are exclusively for local use: 192.168.1.2 and 127.0.0.1. I
think he may be right (these IP numbers are in the "statistics" window that
appears when I click the Xitami icon) and that the solution is to get Xitami
to recognize my changing IP, hence my question about DDNS.

Thank you.
Carl
www.elitz.com



From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Nov  5 01:17:28 2001

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Nov  6 06:56:59 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (M.A.Born)
Date: Tue, 06 Nov 2001 07:56:59 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] SSI question
References: <LAW2-OE39PZXCTPjWvH00007bd7@hotmail.com>

You can use syntax similar to <!--#Include virtual="whatever.file" --> 
to include any file in your pages. For more on Xitami and SSI, check: 
http://www.imatix.com/html/xitami/index6.htm

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Nov  6 12:40:43 2001

Subject: [Xitami] help on alias
Message-ID: <000e01c166c0$40ff1f20$bd8868d5@oemcomputer>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_000B_01C166C0.403EDC60
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

The [Alias] Section
This section lets you define multiple document roots. Each alias =
specifies a name and a path. For example:=20

[Alias]
cdrom=3DG:\html
private/pub=3Di:\pub
private/doc=3Di:\docs\current

The alias name may contain '/'. It is not case sensitive. In A URL, the =
alias comes at the start, e.g.:=20

http://127.0.0.1/cdrom/index.htm

There is no fixed limit to the number of aliases you can define. =
However, if you define large numbers of aliases, Xitami will run slower. =
An alias can refer to a file, including extension. In this case, the =
file will act as a default file for that alias.=20
I've tried to follow the above, but don't know wether what I've put =
below is correct.
I'm trying to getthe browser to read an image from a file that lives in =
the cgi-bin. but all I get is an emmpty place holder where the image is =
suppose to be.
images=3Dc:\images\        http://127.0.0.1/c:/images/.gif/.jpg./.png
Dai
http://www.dezineasite.co.uk
http://www.crazybiker.f2s.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Nov  6 12:41:01 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Simon McVittie)
Date: Tue, 06 Nov 2001 12:41:01 +0000
Subject: [Xitami] how to configure alias
In-Reply-To: Your message of "Tue, 06 Nov 2001 11:19:17 GMT."
 <004401c166b4$e08bf6a0$698c68d5@oemcomputer>
References: <004401c166b4$e08bf6a0$698c68d5@oemcomputer>
Message-ID: <E1615XJ-0006yo-00@entropy.ucam.org>

> I'm using xitami under win98 and I've been playing with some esp. 
> scripts http://www.escapade.org  these scriptslive in the cgi-bin, but 
> the images live in a directory outside the cgi-bin
> http://localhost/cgi-bin/esp.exe?PAGE=abcwebsite2.esp like so, but any 
> images which are part of the script don't show in the browser when 
> called using relative url's in the script.
> E.G. this renders a place holder and no imge in the browser
> <IMG SRC="../../../images/bevel_bg.jpg" BORDER="0" WIDTH="150" 
> HEIGHT="40" ALIGN="bottom" ALT="">

This URL means "start from the current folder /cgi-bin/ (because the SRC 
doesn't start with "/"), go up 3 levels (../../../), go into the images/ 
folder, and get bevel_bg.jpg". You can't go up 3 levels from /cgi-bin/ 
because when you go up 1 level you get to the root folder, /, and you can't 
go up a level again from /; so you certainly can't go up 2 levels!

I'd suggest replacing all your image paths with something like 
SRC="/espimages/bevel_bg.jpg" which will go to the server root, then go 
into an espimages/ subfolder, then download bevel_bg.jpg; then put your 
images in an espimages subfolder of your web pages root (e.g. 
c:\xitami\webpages\espimages on a default install). (Xitami uses the images 
subdirectory already, for its own built-in images like the directory 
listing icons)

If you insist on using relative URLs, remember that they all have to be 
relative to where your CGI script is, i.e. relative to the cgi-bin folder.

Also remember that they're URLs and not file paths: if your cgi-bin is in 
c:\xitami\cgi-bin, you can't get to c:\images with ../../images/ - the "up 
one level" is handled by the user's Web browser, which has no idea where 
stuff is on your hard disk.

I realise this isn't particularly clear, so here's a silly example:

Suppose your server is set up with an alias for /docs/, as follows:

- / points to c:\xitami\webpages, like the default setup
- /cgi-bin/ points to c:\xitami\cgi-bin, again like the default setup
- /docs/ points to d:\my documents\public_html

Suppose you're looking at this site in a Web browser, and you're looking at 
http://myserver/docs/MyPlanToTakeOverTheWorld.html. When you go to this 
page, Xitami will look up what /docs/ means and return the contents of 
d:\my documents\public_html\MyPlanToTakeOverTheWorld.html. If this file 
contains a hyperlink to "../MoreRanting.html", you might expect that to 
mean d:\my documents\MoreRanting.html.

However, the ../ is resolved by the web browser, not the server. All the 
web browser knows is that it's at a server called http://myserver, in a 
folder called /docs/, looking at HereIsARant.html. So, it takes the current 
folder (/docs/), goes up one level (to /), and downloads MoreRanting.html 
from that folder - that's http://myserver/MoreRanting.html.

Xitami looks up what / means, looks for a file called MoreRanting.html, and 
dutifully returns c:\xitami\webpages\MoreRanting.html.

This is good, because it means there's no way a web browser can get at 
documents in folders you haven't specifically added to the server. For 
example, if it worked the way you seem to have assumed, the browser could 
request http://myserver/../defaults.aut and get c:\xitami\defaults.aut. 
This would be bad, because defaults.aut is a list of usernames and 
passwords for the password-protected pages on your server, if you have 
any... don't worry though, this doesn't actually happen.

For the same reason, to get a hyperlink to something you've stored in 
webpages from a script in cgi-bin, you just go "../something" or 
"/something", not "../webpages/something" - and to get from webpages to 
cgi-bin, you just go "cgi-bin" and not "../cgi-bin" (this would make no 
sense because you're already at the root as far as a web browser is 
concerned, so you can't go up any further).

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Nov  6 15:56:28 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Simon McVittie)
Date: Tue, 06 Nov 2001 15:56:28 +0000
Subject: [Xitami] how to configure alias
In-Reply-To: Your message of "Tue, 06 Nov 2001 13:02:37 GMT."
 <001d01c166c3$7078b7e0$bd8868d5@oemcomputer>
References: <004401c166b4$e08bf6a0$698c68d5@oemcomputer>
 <E1615XJ-0006yo-00@entropy.ucam.org>  <001d01c166c3$7078b7e0$bd8868d5@oemcomputer>
Message-ID: <E1618aS-0000Eb-00@entropy.ucam.org>

> I'm testing things localy on my pc not on the host server and when I go
> insert an imasge from the image folder it goes back 3 levels as so
> <IMG SRC="../../../images/bevel_bg.jpg" BORDER="0" WIDTH="150" HEIGHT="40"
> ALIGN="bottom" ALT="">
> now al I want is to confige the alias to read any images from this folder on
> my c:drive
> is this correct if not can you give the correct configuration
> images=c:\images\        http://127.0.0.1/c:/images/.gif/.jpg./.png

If you're running Xitami on your PC, that *is* the host server. Your web 
browser (Internet Explorer, Netscape, whatever) doesn't read from the disk 
itself if you're testing your site through Xitami - all it knows about your 
site is what Xitami tells it.

If you set an alias like 

[Alias]
images=c:\images

then, for example, going to the URL http://127.0.0.1/images/bevel_bg.jpg 
will get you the contents of the file 'c:\images\bevel_bg.jpg'. (* footnote)

In general, an alias like

[Alias]
aliased/server/path=c:\real\path\on\disk

will map the URL 
http://127.0.0.1/aliased/server/path/somefolder/somefile.ext
to the real file 
c:\real\path\on\disk\somefolder\somefile.ext
(I hope you can see where the the components of this path come from).

It sounds as though your HTML writing software is getting its relative 
paths wrong, or making big assumptions about how your real disk filesystem 
maps to the server's "virtual filesystem". If the current working directory 
is '/cgi-bin', which it is for these scripts, your web browser *can't* go 
up 3 levels, because as far as it can see there's only one level to go up 
through (it goes up one level to '/', then can't see any further).

If you have an alias like the one above you can use an image with a tag like

<img src="../images/bevel.jpg" alt="">

which your web browser will expand to
http://127.0.0.1/cgi-bin/../images/bevel.jpg
then contract to
http://127.0.0.1/images/bevel.jpg
before it sends 
the request.

It may be better to use an absolute path like

<img src="/images/bevel.jpg" alt=""> (this one is probably better),

which your web browser will expand to http://127.0.0.1/images/bevel.jpg 
before it sends the request.

It's impossible to go up 3 levels because your browser doesn't know there's 
anything above the root, so it won't send a request which goes above /; and 
because, for security reasons, Xitami won't send files from outside the 
webpages root, unless it's been told to do so by an alias. This is to 
prevent arbitrary users doing things like sending a request for something 
like http://127.0.0.1/../../windows/system/user.dat and getting half your 
Registry.


*: Xitami assumes your 'images' directory contains the icons which come 
with it (this isn't great design IMO, but that's how it works). If you want 
directory listings to look right, you might need to copy the images from 
c:\xitami\webpages\images (or wherever you have Xitami installed) into the 
folder which will be accessible as http://127.0.0.1/images/ (e.g. 
c:\images).

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Nov  6 17:45:23 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Simon McVittie)
Date: Tue, 06 Nov 2001 17:45:23 +0000
Subject: [Xitami] how to configure alias
In-Reply-To: Your message of "Tue, 06 Nov 2001 16:54:56 GMT."
 <000d01c166e3$c4dfdfa0$849368d5@oemcomputer>
References: <004401c166b4$e08bf6a0$698c68d5@oemcomputer>
 <E1615XJ-0006yo-00@entropy.ucam.org> <001d01c166c3$7078b7e0$bd8868d5@oemcomputer> <E1618aS-0000Eb-00@entropy.ucam.org>  <000d01c166e3$c4dfdfa0$849368d5@oemcomputer>
Message-ID: <E161AHs-0000S1-00@entropy.ucam.org>

> Based on the info below is it possible for you to send me the paths that I
> put in both alias boxes so that when I insert an image <IMG
> SRC="../../../images/masthead.gif" BORDER="0" WIDTH="600" HEIGHT="100"
> ALIGN="bottom" ALT="">it will work
> 
> C:\Xitami\cgi-bin\esp-pages  This is the path to the folder which holds the
> files
> 
> C:\images  this is the path to the images folder

No, not really. The best way to make this work is to change the src 
attribute of the <IMG> tags to /images/whatever.gif. If you use an 
automatic program like Frontpage or Dreamweaver or something to make your 
HTML, either hand-edit the <IMG> tags or get a different automatic program.
Relative paths (especially ones with .. in them) are generally good for 
simple hierarchical sites where everything goes in one folder (i.e. pure 
HTML/images sites) and bad for sites with CGI, aliases, or anything else 
advanced.

The rest of this e-mail describes a hack to make it behave like you ask for 
- it probably isn't a good idea though, because it's a very weird 
configuration and will break as soon as you upload it to any other server 
(i.e. any computer not running your personal hand-configured copy of 
Xitami) - so if you upload your pages to your ISP's web server, or a 
commercial web host, or basically any computer you don't actually have 
physical access to, it won't work. Consider very carefully whether this is 
what you want...

*** If you want a reasonably normal server, look away now ;-) ***






It's _possible_ to do what you're asking by using an extra alias to 
deliberately "move" ESP deeper into the site hierarchy. See the notes 
above, and note that if you later decide you want to move your site to your 
ISP or commercial host's server, IT WON'T WORK so don't ask me to fix it.

Exactly what you do depends on the URL to your script, not the folder the 
content is kept in. Web browsers don't know that your pages are in 
c:\xitami\cgi-bin\esp-pages (how would they?), but they do know the URL 
they just used to get at the script which serves the pages.

If the ***URL for your script*** is currently something like
http://127.0.0.1/cgi-bin/myscript?page=mypage
then you could do:

-- begin cfg section
[Alias]
images=c:\images

[Cgi-Alias]
cgi-bin/esp/esp=c:\Xitami\cgi-bin
-- end cfg section

and tell people that the new URL is:
http://127.0.0.1/cgi-bin/esp/esp/myscript?page=mypage

(note the two completely pointless esp "folders", to make sure going up 3 
levels gets you somewhere sensible)

Or, if the ***URL for your script***  is currently something like
http://127.0.0.1/cgi-bin/esp-pages/myscript?page=mypage
then you could do:

-- begin cfg section
[Alias]
images=c:\images

[Cgi-Alias]
cgi-bin/esp/esp-pages=c:\Xitami\cgi-bin\esp-pages
-- end cfg section

and tell people that the new URL is:
http://127.0.0.1/cgi-bin/esp/esp-pages/myscript?page=mypage

Neither of these is a clever idea. Don't use them if you want your server 
to be anywhere near normal.

Does your file have an extension of  '.ssi', '.shtm', or
'.shtml'? If not it won't work. If it does then a statement
as below or like <!--#include virtual="rexxdate.htm"-->
should include the referenced file. The
virtual="whatever.file" is the path relative to the html
page that contains it, or an absolute path, and they are
server paths, starting from, and within server-root.

It works for me. I am running v2.5b4 on NT 4.0 SP4. Maybe
you need to upgrade to a newer version?

Good Luck!
Dennis

Not quite.

if you add the alias

images_esp=c:\xitami\images_esp\

then to link to an image called filename.gif in that directory, you would
use:

http://127.0.0.1/images_esp/filename.gif

In other words, the alias *replaces* the actual directory.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Nov  6 22:29:24 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Bowden, Russell)
Date: Tue, 06 Nov 2001 16:29:24 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] The LRWP protocol
Message-ID: <EX-20011106-163507-0001@exchange.fiserv-missive1.fiserv.net>

I've been using LRWP for a couple of years and it works fine.
To answer your questions:

1. Yes, you should certainly make the LRWP programs executable.  You will
need to run them.  They are not executed by Xitami.  They connect to Xitami
via a socket (port xx81).

2.  I don't think it matters where you put them.  Mine are in a directory
which also contains the Xitami directory.

3.  I don't know about WBA, but look in Xitami.cfg.  LRWP is probably already
enabled by default

If you try out the examples I don't think you will have any trouble.  The only
thing I had to do special was to modify lrwplib.c somewhat to make it more
"COBOL-friendly", since most of our stuff is COBOL.

Good luck.

Russell

Greetings;

with the alias you have below the url would be
http://127.0.0.1/images_esp/something.gif and so on.

No matter where the actual path points to you only use the
alias in the url. And you can't use .. and such to get out
of the tree under the alias. You need to experiment with
simple scripts and simple pages so you can quickly see what
works and what doesn't.

> as below or like <!--#include virtual="rexxdate.htm"-->

> virtual="whatever.file" is the path relative to the html
> page that contains it, or an absolute path, and they are
> server paths, starting from, and within server-root.
>
> It works for me. I am running v2.5b4 on NT 4.0 SP4. Maybe
> you need to upgrade to a newer version?

I'm not sure if this counts as a bug or a feature :-/ but you will 
generally find it better to always use forward slashes in the Xitami files

I.e. do images_esp=c:/xitami/images_esp/

Francis
PS the only place where this appears to be untrue is in the GSL script 
processing where .xml FILESPEC seems to have to be done using \
PPS Just curious is anyone else using GSL/XML with Xitami? It seems to 
be way faster than perl / CGI once you get the files in the right format 
- but its lacking a few features such as a index(string, substring) and 
the modulo operator. I *think* I've figured out what to change to fix 
this and would be willing to submit changes if other people are 
interested...

>when I go to enter images_esp=c:\xitami\images_esp\ in the alias box all

>>>

try handediting the defaults.cfg file in c:\xitami . Under the [alias] 
section add the line you want
( images_esp=c:/xitami/images_esp/") note using /es not \es!

For example I just did this
Vnc = "c:/xitami/vnc_docs/"
to test and it worked fine

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Nov  7 18:06:05 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Wed, 07 Nov 2001 19:06:05 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] BUG ./webpages required
Message-ID: <3BE9780D.4030005@freesbee.fr>

Interesting bug with 2.5b4 and 2.5b5 (haven't checked any 2.4 versions) 
- within the folder where you installed Xitami (e.g. c:\xitami) you must 
have a directory called webpages even if your web root is somewhere 
completely different (such as D:\webroot). As far as I can see the 
/xitami/webpages directory can be empty but it must exist!

Francis
PS running on Win ME and Win 2k

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Nov  7 16:55:51 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Wed, 07 Nov 2001 17:55:51 +0100
Subject: Disclaimers (Was: [Xitami] CGI Scripting)
Message-ID: <45670@dsl.co.uk>

In message <000001c16468$503b3b40$6400000a@techapp.co.uk>
   "David Lambert" writes:

> Thanks you all for the replies, including those concerning the disclaimer.
> It's part and parcel of living in the UK now, where privacy laws are under
> considerable threat. Our govt. likes to snoop, so does your but they haven't
> told you yet!

Nevertheless, including such a disclaimer on mails sent on the one-to-many
basis of a mailing list is consummately stupid, because YOU have no
control over the members of the set which your disclaimer calls "intended
recipients", since members may join and leave the list at any time, and
in most cases any legislation upon which you are relying is positively
NOT applicable to the "recipients".

I would advise anyone with such boilerplate inclusions to configure their
mailers so as NOT to send it when the addressee is a mailing list; ditto
for postings to newsgroups, where such disclaimers are equally risible.

PHBs require educating as to the differing modes in which e-mail might be
used: for them to issue an edict requiring such boilerplate on mails
which are not one-to-one (or one-to-few) merely reinforces just why they
ARE pointy-haired bosses.

[Catching upon on some hundreds of posts to the list that have occurred
during my brief visit to .cy]

Hi i have had this problem in the past sometimes its the vh wizard not
coping with the length of the name ...which means you have to edit the file
manually.
the thing i found that fixed the problem many many versions back was to set
up aliases for the hosted domains as well.

i have ,since then, done this each time i set up a new domain and short of
the odd spelling error, never had a problem since.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Nov  9 00:06:38 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Thu, 08 Nov 2001 19:06:38 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] A problem with Xitami Web Server
References: <LAEDKBKIPJGPNKLDJHCDMEBBCBAA.jordan.arribas@innovatec.nu>
Message-ID: <3BEB1E0E.78645414@rci.rutgers.edu>

> You can try in http://wwwgssr.uah.es/cg-bin/contador.exe

The first "i" in "cgi-bin" in the URL you posted isn't a plain "i" but
has an accute accent over it. You probably want a plain "i" in the URL. 

http://wwwgssr.uah.es/cgi-bin/contador.exe "works" for me, EXCEPT it
DOWNLOADED your EXE program to MY machine! I don't want it, and you
probably don't want everybody to have it. 

Re-check your cgi-bin settings. CGI programs should go in someplace like
C:\Xitami\cgi-bin, _OUTSIDE_ the Web-root folder C:\Xitami\webpages. Set
the CGI options so files in that CGI directory can only be executed, NOT
downloaded directly. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Nov  9 00:26:39 2001

Hello!
 
> My CGI is wrotten with C, simple and standard C. The program 
> is right, but I

In your html file there is a string

<!-- #exec cmd="http://wwwgssr.uah.es/cgi-bin/contador" -->

First feel the difference between cgi and server side includes (ssi).

If you use ssi, then this string can be like a
<!-- #exec cmd="C:/web/cgi-bin/contador.exe" -->
As you see there is a LOCAL path not remote.

And you must configure your Xitami and system to operate with ssi.

Best wishes!

  Andris

> <?
> require("fileupload.class");
> 
> #--------------------------------#
> # Variables
> #--------------------------------#
> 
> // The path to the directory where you want the
> // uploaded files to be saved. This MUST end with a
> // trailing slash unless you use $PATH = ""; to
> // upload to the current directory. Whatever
> directory
> // you choose, please chmod 777 that directory.
> 
> 	$PATH = "./images/";
> 
> // The name of the file field in your form.
> 
> 	$FILENAME = "userfile";
> 
> // ACCEPT mode - if you only want to accept
> // a certain type of file.
> // possible file types that PHP recognizes includes:
> //
> // OPTIONS INCLUDE:
> //  text/plain
> //  image/gif
> //  image/jpeg
> //  image/png
> 
> 	$ACCEPT = "";
> 
> // If no extension is supplied, and the browser or
> PHP
> // can not figure out what type of file it is, you
> can
> // add a default extension - like ".jpg" or ".txt"
> 
> 	$EXTENSION = "";
> 
> // SAVE_MODE: if your are attempting to upload
> // a file with the same name as another file in the
> // $PATH directory
> //
> // OPTIONS:
> //   1 = overwrite mode
> //   2 = create new with incremental extention
> //   3= do nothing if exists, highest protection
> 
> 	$SAVE_MODE = 1;
> 
> 
> #--------------------------------#
> # PHP
> #--------------------------------#
> 
> function print_file($file, $type, $mode) {
> 	if($file) {
> 		if(ereg("image", $type)) {
> 			echo "<img src=\"" . $file . "\" border=\"0\"
> alt=\"\">";
> 		}
> 		else {
> 			$userfile = fopen($file, "r");
> 			while(!feof($userfile)) {
> 				$line = fgets($userfile, 255);
> 				switch($mode){
> 					case 1:
> 						echo $line;
> 						break;
> 					case 2:
> 						echo nl2br(ereg_replace("\t",
> "&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;",
> htmlentities($line)));
> 						break;
> 				}
> 			}
> 		}
> 	}
> }
> 
> $upload = new uploader;
> $upload->max_filesize(500000);
> 
> if($upload->upload("$FILENAME", "$ACCEPT",
> "$EXTENSION")) {
> 	while(list($key, $var) = each($upload->file)){
> 		echo $key . " = " . $var . "<br>";
> 	}
> 	if($upload->save_file("$PATH", $SAVE_MODE)) {
> 		print("<p>Saved as: " . $upload->new_file .
> "<p>");
> 		print_file($upload->new_file,
> $upload->file["type"], 2);
> 	}
> }
> 
> if($upload->errors) {
> 	while(list($key, $var) = each($upload->errors)){
> 		echo "<p>" . $var . "<br>";
> 	}
> }
> 
> if ($NEW_NAME) {
> 	print("<p>Name of sent file:
> <b>$NEW_NAME</b></p>");
> }

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Nov  9 16:38:04 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 09 Nov 2001 11:38:04 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Upload scripts on Xitami
References: <20011109082915.99269.qmail@web20001.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <3BEC066C.768C9607@rci.rutgers.edu>

> problems making it work. 

What happens? 

> how do I do a chmod on Xitami on WindowsXP

You don't.

What permissions do you want? 

Windows does not have the eXecutable flag so that is not needed (as it
would be on unix). Xitami uses rules similar to DOS to decide if a file
can be executed. First: Xitami will run scripts only in certain
directories, typically c:\xitami\cgi-bin. Then it looks for EXE, COM or
BAT extension (the closest DOS comes to an X flag). Xitami also examines
for the "MZ" header that marks a true EXE file (but COM files must be
loaded on blind faith). If the file appears to be text and isn't BAT, it
looks for "perl" in the first #! line and calls Perl either at the
specified place or by tracing PATH. 

 -PRR

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Bob Paddock)
Date: Sat, 10 Nov 2001 11:13:22 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] I need a page hit counter
Message-ID: <200111101113984.SM00351@there>

I'm looking for a Page Hit counter, a simple text based one to show the 
number of times the page has been visited to the visitor.

I've looked through the archives and see this is a frequent question, but all 
of the links that I tried pointed to broken or non-relevant links (some of 
the messages where from 1999).

Also the URL given in the FAQ for this question does not work any more either.

All of the counter programs I've found so far require DOCUMENT_URI to be set
in the environment, and Xitami does not support this.

So how do you do a counter in Xitami?

>> All environment variables are available to CGI programs, if this
>> option is not disabled.
>
>Then I must have some thing disabled that I don't know what to turn
>on:
>
>Running the 'testcgi' program does NOT show enviroment variable called
>DOCUMENT_URI.

Okay, I've double-checked. Xitami does not set the DOCUMENT_URI 
variable for CGI programs. You'll have to find a web counter that 
does not use this. I suggest you ask the discussion group to see if 
anyone has one they prefer.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Nov 10 18:45:10 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Dwaine Gonyier)
Date: Sat, 10 Nov 2001 13:45:10 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] I need a page hit counter
References: <200111101113984.SM00351@there>

I use Count from http://www.muquit.com/muquit/software/Count/Count.html

This is not a text only counter, though.  It is a CGI-based counter that
dynamically creates a GIF image for the hit count. It has a lot of options
and is very configurable.  I have been using it for a while and it seems
to work pretty well with Xitami 2.5b5

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Nov 11 12:00:44 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael)
Date: Sun, 11 Nov 2001 07:00:44 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami Crashing with Norton AV
In-Reply-To: <200110050320.PAA04044@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
References: Message from bhk@dsl.co.uk (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})    of "Tue, 25 Sep 2001 18:49:24 +0100." <45172@dsl.co.uk>
Message-ID: <3BEE221C.1469.281A90@localhost>

I haven't seen this posted.

Xitami v2.5b5
Norton AntiVirus v4.05
WindowsXP/98/95

If I do a network virus check using Norton, any machine on the lan 
running Xitami will often (not always) lock up.  In WindowsXP only 
Xitami has to be restarted.  The local machine running Xitami and 
Norton never locks up.

I  noticed this when I began running Norton automatically at night and 
the next morning I would have to restart servers.  Without Xitami and 
Norton both runing there is never a problem.

There have been no viruses. (Knock on silicon.)

This version of Norton is one of the last forever free network capable 
versions.  The virus definitions have to be updated manually but free is 
better than a yearly fee.

Regards,

Michael

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Nov 11 18:28:38 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (alexandre schneider)
Date: Sun, 11 Nov 2001 19:28:38 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Servlets
References: <5C97A373607ED31188CD002048406DEE04B6E8C9@lsv-msg05.stortek.com>
Message-ID: <005401c16ae0$05bbb210$7909e4d5@marsupilami>

You can place your servlets anywhere but you have to put their path into
your CLASSPATH variable. And don't forget to run servletrunner of course.

In my case, i've created an directory called java under c:\xitami\ and I
located in this place the servletrunner and a directory called "servlets".
This directory is put in the classpath; and it works.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Nov 12 09:01:53 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Fabian Bess)
Date: Mon, 12 Nov 2001 10:01:53 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] $PHP_SELF variable
Message-ID: <3BEF9001.1040705@gmx.net>

I have a problem with the $PHP_SELF variable. Since Version 2.4d5 (or d4 
I'm not sure) this PHP variable which should be filled with the calling 
script's filename is empty. It seems that Xitami doesn't hand over the 
information needed by PHP to fill this variable.
For a while I used $SCRIPT_NAME instead but it's a bit uncomfortable 
because I have to edit all scripts before uploading them to my host due 
to his configuration where this variable is filled with the path to PHP 
itself.
This problem started occuring with the obove mentioned version d4 or d5 
of Xitami. Before that $PHP_SELF was fully available.

Any other idea to get around this or how to get $PHP_SELF to work agian?

Thx
-- 
Fabian Bess (webmaster@tannenhof.de)
Webmaster Drogenhilfe Tannenhof Berlin e.V. 'http://www.tannenhof.de'

Seems like I'm the only one having this problem...
currently this is how I'm solving this problem:

$serv = $SERVER_SOFTWARE;
function OwnName() {
 global $serv;
 if($serv == "Xitami") return true;
}

and

<FORM action="<?php if(OwnName()) { echo $SCRIPT_NAME; } else { echo 
$PHP_SELF; }; ?>" method="POST">

for some reason you can't test for $SERVER_SOFTWARE directly

maybe there's still another sollution out there?!

> itself.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Nov 12 18:46:23 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 12 Nov 2001 13:46:23 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] $PHP_SELF variable
References: <3BEF9001.1040705@gmx.net>
Message-ID: <3BF018FF.77C316F1@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  Since Version 2.4d5 (or d4 I'm not sure) this PHP variable which should be filled with the calling script's filename is empty. 

Which Version Of PHP ???

The current version of PHP changed which variable it uses to find its
script. The PHP site documents this as a security issue. Xitami does not
(AFAIK, never did) fill this variable.

I had a BAT file which patched this under DOS/Win. It was posted here
last year. Unfortunately I lost most of my older messages since then. I
*think* the trick is to SET PATH_INFO the same as SCRIPT_PATH and then
call PHP. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Nov 13 02:00:46 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Stephen Roberts)
Date: Mon, 12 Nov 2001 21:00:46 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Dynamic IP... is anyone else using it?
In-Reply-To: <AIEJLJENNEEGIDEIELPGEEIBCAAA.reds@chicagonet.net>
Message-ID: <0f6bf5457010db1NYCSMTP1@nyc.rr.com>

Carl my IP address is dynamic also.  I am also using TZO to resolve the 
dynamic IP issue and have been successful in running Xitami behind a 
router.  I never bothered to setup the DDNS feature in Xitami since I am 
already running the TZO client on my server.  Since I am on a network and 
behind a router I am also using a DNS server which allows me to 
access "MYDomain.com" from any pc on my network.  "Simple DNS' located at 
http://www.jhsoft.com/ offers a solution for this, remember also that if 
you're using a router you will have to map port 80 to the machine that 
you're running Xitami on.

Stephen.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Nov 13 05:16:53 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Carl J. Elitz)
Date: Mon, 12 Nov 2001 23:16:53 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] Dynamic IP... is anyone else using it?
In-Reply-To: <0f6bf5457010db1NYCSMTP1@nyc.rr.com>
Message-ID: <AIEJLJENNEEGIDEIELPGMEIGCAAA.reds@chicagonet.net>

The only feature I have not been able to implement with Xitami using the TZO
client is FTP. I was trying to get the integrated DDNS function in Xitami to
work only because I thought it might resolve my FTP problem. Perhaps my real
problem with FTP is that I am also behind a router? Any help you could give
me with that issue, Stephen, -or anyone else-, would be greatly appreciated.

ROUTER ISSUE:

My machine, like Stephen's machine, is part of a netork, but only a small
one consisting of my machine and another machine used to play occassional
two-player games. All unsolicited internet traffic is routed to my main
machine - as determined by a setting in the router software. Can anyone
suggest a reason why the Xitami web server works to serve web pages to
people outside my network, but won't work to serve FTP? The TZO tech support
people have been nice, but unable to help with this, suggesting that the
problem may be my Xitami settings. They say that their FTP client keeps
getting 192.168.1.2 as my machine's IP address (my machine's local IP) when
they hit my site (when the TZO client is running), instead of the dynamic
address assigned by my ISP.

I have read everything I can about my router, but have found no obvious
settings which would tell it to treat FTP traffic in a certain way. The
router is a 3Com router and is configured via a web page interface, so the
emphasis of the router software is on keeping things simple. I was concerned
that the router wasn't designed to do what I'm doing in mind, but the good
news is that I have found that I can telnet to my router's IP address, and
that there are many "unimplemented" text commands that can change the
router's settings, if necessary. I would obviously rather run just Xitami if
possible, rather than Xitami and the TZO client.

DDNS ISSUE:

The router may be the ultimate solution to my problem, but even so, it does
not explain why the Xitami DDNS feature is not working with TZO, or explain
the rather cryptic error messages I am getting from Xitami. I am still
curious about that. I don't think this feature is well implemented.

DNS SERVER:

Thanks, Stephen, for the suggestion about http://www.jhsoft.com/. I reviewed
the pages there, but don't think this is an issue for me. As I understand
it, a DNS server would be something I would be interested in if I had a lot
of machines on my side of the router, right? My current network setting in
Windows ME is "DNS disabled."

TESTING MY OWN WEB PAGE/FTP PAGE:

Finally, someone told me that, because I was behind a router, I simply
cannot visit my own machine through the internet. In other words, although I
can hit http://192.168.1.2 or "trick" my machine into taking me to my own
web page by mapping my domain to this IP through the "hosts" file, there is
no way for me to test my site as people on the other side of the router
would see it. This has been very frustrating because Xitami works
beautifully on this side of the router. It's only when I get involved in the
dynamic IP stuff that things don't work.

I've been playing with this for more than 3 weeks now with almost no luck.
It's been really frustrating, so I REALLY appreciate any help I get on this.
The thing that has me most confused is that the Web pages serve, the FTP
won't. What gives?

Thanks.

-Carl.

Ok now look at you shebang line if perl is
set in your PATH you can use
#! perl -Tw
use strict;
use CGI::Carp "fatalsToBrowser";
print "Context-Type: image/\n\n"; #should be the first
#thing that gets printed
500 is an internal server error and usually
a syntax error is the cause see if is will run
from the command prompt

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Nov 13 09:15:55 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Tue, 13 Nov 2001 10:15:55 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Dynamic IP... is anyone else using it?
References: <AIEJLJENNEEGIDEIELPGMEIGCAAA.reds@chicagonet.net>
Message-ID: <3BF0E4CB.5040700@freesbee.fr>

I think what you have is an FTP client problem related to Network 
Address Translation (NAT). It is not a DDNS problem a Xitami problem as 
it will occur with other FTP servers.

Try getting a remote machine to run a very simple client (e.g. the CLI 
ftp client included with windows 9x). It should have no problem, whereas 
the funky GUI client may fail. I have seen this behavious with Netscape 
4.x and believe it also occurs with other clients. The problem is this:

Netscape's FTP client issues a command (SYST I think) to the FTP server 
to tell it what IP address it has and then tries to connect to that IP 
address for future connections. This is stupid because the FTP cleint 
already has an IP address that works. Of course this IP address is 
embedded within the message so the NAT s/w on the router doesn't modify it.

The way to check this is (assuming the simple DOS ftp worked) is to look 
and see if the GUI client does a SYST command or not and what the 
response is.

Francis

>Currently running the console ver of 2.5b5. In previous releases of 
>Xitami the NT service version has lagged the console version and had 
>bugs that were fixed by the console version.

It's "lagged" behind only because the binary wasn't rebuilt properly.

The Xitami 2.5b5 _beta_ was built with the same source code for all the
different build versions, so should be basically identical for all of
them.

>Is there anyone running the service version of 2.5b5 who can say whetehr 
>the same applies to this version. I'm probably going use the service 
>version as I move to production anyway,  

Keep in mind that 2.5b5 is a beta version and does have known bugs; if
you're going to use it in production carefully check none of those are
going to bite you.

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Nov 13 23:45:06 2001

Subject: [Xitami] $PHP_SELF variable
Message-ID: <4A256B03.00827BC9.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>

--0__=8M7op4MRVL1Zv4mEu0fS8SQh96FFLWW20Fq1q0xVQxPncZYpiO0U01G2
Content-type: text/plain; charset="us-ascii"
Content-Disposition: inline




Just a little something that I used when I came across this difference between
Apache & Xitami. This will run
on either Apache or Xitami, I didn't wrap it in a function as it is only
executed once at the beginning of a new
session in my application.

Hope you find this of some help.

        $session->RootPath = stripSlashes( dirname( $PATH_TRANSLATED));     //
Assume we are in the root dir
        $session->BasePath = basename( $session->RootPath);
// Assume we are one directory below the resource root
        if( strlen( trim($PHP_SELF))) $session->BaseURL = dirname( $PHP_SELF);
// & that this matches BasePath - this works with Apache
        else   // Xitami  ???
        {
     // This works for Xitami
               $url = parse_url($HTTP_REFERER);
               $session->BaseURL = dirname( $url["path"]);
        }

Regards, Paul Shortis

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Nov 14 02:17:34 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 13 Nov 2001 21:17:34 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] $PHP_SELF variable
References: <3BEF9001.1040705@gmx.net> <3BF018FF.77C316F1@rci.rutgers.edu> <3BF0CBA4.30900@gmx.net>
Message-ID: <3BF1D43E.C6424780@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  describe this a little more in detail to me? Not on the list but in private?

I'm not being secretive--- I just don't have my notes handy. It
is a fairly common issue here so (now that I am at the machine
with my hacks) I will reply here. 

In Defaults.cfg: 

 [Filter]
    .php=C:/php/patchphp.bat

patchphp.bat is: 

 @set path_translated=%1
 @C:\php\php.exe

Notes: 

When Xitami sees a ".php" file, it calls the BAT file which sets
the environment variable and then calls PHP.exe. 

I found this was needed for PHP 4, was not needed for PHP 3. 

If you use other extensions for PHP scripts, you will need more
entries in Defaults.cfg.

The "@" prevents DOS from writing to output. (I hate to do that,
but DOS's gibberish confuses things.)

Forward/slash in Xitami config files; back\slash in DOS. (Both
places *may* work the other way... but this is the preferred
syntax for unix-think Xitami and DOS-think Windows.)

I assume "C:" drive and the customary installation directories.
Adapt to your situation. 

 -PRR

Frances Turner wrote:

>I think what you have is an FTP client problem related to Network
>Address Translation (NAT). The problem is this:

>Netscape's FTP client issues a command (SYST I think) to the FTP server
>to tell it what IP address it has and then tries to connect to that IP
>address for future connections. This is stupid because the FTP cleint
>already has an IP address that works. Of course this IP address is
>embedded within the message so the NAT s/w on the router doesn't modify it.

I ran my copy of LeechFTP, a simple windows-based client to test Frances's
theory. Indeed, I did see that the software issued a SYST command. Of
course, on my side of the router, it doesn't cause any problems. It is only
a problem for people on the outside of my network.

BTW, the possibility that the FTP client was causing the server to send my
internal IP is the original reason why I wanted to bag the TZO "IP catching"
client software and use xitami's imbedded client to retreive the IP. My
thought was that Xitami would pass the correct IP to the FTP server and
would send to the requesting FTP client my true "internet" IP, instead of
the IP I use on this side of the router.

One user reported that he could upload to me, but not download from me. This
is the person that reported seeing my local IP address, instead of my global
address as he should have seen it. Frances, is this consistent with your
diagnosis? Do you think there is a solution? Anyone else have any ideas?

Thanks.

-Carl.

It sounds to me like your TZO client may be sending your router mapped IP, I
say this because if they are saying that they get that common network IP
address as the resolved address, it would have to be comming from TZO as
reported to them via client.  Perhaps a matter of the TZO client needing to
know what IP to be providing via the client.  (isp vs network).   I really
see no other way they would see your network IP externally.

You can test this theory by going to the control panel at TZO and placing
your current ISP address manually into the given entry field they provide
for doing this manually- (turn off the tzo client so it doesn't override it
again).

See if it then works- If you want to contact me via email directly it may
prove faster- I've run xitami, and about everything under the sun with my
TZO setup so I'm sure we could find the issue with a few wacks at it.

This doesn't take into account any mapping you may need to do for ports, but
I'm not sure that's even your issue here.

Jack

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Nov 15 03:17:26 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Carl J. Elitz)
Date: Wed, 14 Nov 2001 21:17:26 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] Dynamic IP... is anyone else using it? --> PASV FTP fails inbound through NAT
In-Reply-To: <005001c16d34$11739900$0300a8c0@test>
Message-ID: <AIEJLJENNEEGIDEIELPGGEIMCAAA.reds@chicagonet.net>

PASV FTP FAILS INBOUND THROUGH NAT

To those who may have been following this thread and trying to help me
figure out why I can't get FTP to work with Xitami, thank you. I have had a
lot of thoughtful responses. I think I may have a definitive diagnosis for
why I can't get Xitami's FTP server working properly. As always, your
comments are greatly appreciated...

Currently, Internet Explorer and Netscape have built in FTP clients, but
these clients do not use "normal" FTP. Instead, like most of the newer FTP
clients, they use "PASV FTP" which appears to have become the standard FTP
protocol. I found an article by Don Kelloway which explains the problem in
detail better than I ever could.

Don writes the following which is available at
http://war.jgaa.com/ftp/?cmd=show_page&ID=ftp_pasv.

Comments? More importantly... solutions?

-Carl.

---
With regards to the difference between PASV FTP and Normal FTP:

Both PASV FTP and Normal FTP work in the same manner for the initial
"Control Channel" connection, which occurs as follows:

The external user allocates two port numbers for the FTP session.  The first
port number is reflected in the connection that's used to TCP port 21, on
the FTP server.  This is referred to as the "Control or Command Channel".
The usage of the second port number allocated by the external user, as well
as how the connection is established is where the difference occurs...

If the external user sends the FTP server a PORT  (Normal FTP) command,
which also contains the second allocated port number inside the data of the
packet.  Then the FTP server initiates the next connection to the external
user.  This occurs from TCP port 20 (on the FTP server) to whatever the
allocated second port number is.  This is referred to as the "Data Channel"
connection.

If you've noticed, it's the FTP server which initiated the connection
outbound, to the external user.  In the world of security and firewalls,
this can be a very bad thing.  Hence, the reason why PASV FTP was created.
This is also a reason why some FTP servers do not accept the PORT command.

If the user sends the FTP server a PASV (PASV FTP) command, then the FTP
server responds back to the external user with a port number that it has
allocated.  SPECIAL NOTE:  The port number to be used, AS WELL AS the FTP
server's IP Address is embedded inside the data of the packet sent to the
external user.

When the user receives this packet, the external user initiates the "Data
Channel" connection from its second allocated port number, to the IP Address
and port number provided from the FTP server.

See the difference?  In a PASV connection, the "Data Channel" is
initiated/created by the external user.  In a Normal connection, it's
established by the FTP server.

Note: All web browsers use PASV FTP as its means of FTP.  Although I have
heard a rumor that Internet Explorer 5.0 will support both.  I have yet to
confirm this...

Now, let's look at the "Special Note"...

To reiterate, in a PASV FTP session, the FTP server tells the external user
what the FTP servers' IP Address is, as well as what port number to initiate
an inbound connection to.

If you're using NAT (Network Address Translation), the FTP server is
probably going to be an IP Address within the established "Private Range"
(although that really isn't the issue).  Now, say for instance the FTP
server is 192.168.100.10 and an external user is trying to initiate a PASV
FTP session to this FTP server.  Because the IP Address 192.168.100.10 as
well as the port number is embedded inside the packet and because a lot of
NAT implementations cannot "rewrite" this information.  The external user
receives this information and will try to initiate the "Data Channel"
connection to an IP Address (192.168.100.10) that will never leave their
local LAN.  Hence PASV FTP fails inbound through NAT.
---

Figured out that the offending line was a GSL line that said
<A href='/discussion/$(name)/index.xml' TITLE='Click 
Here'><h2>$(Title)</h2></a> 

If I remove the TITLE='...' and have
<A href='/discussion/$(name)/index.xml'><h2>$(Title)</h2></a> 
it works no problem at all!

The only thing I can think of is that I have a XML object with an 
attribute the same  name as a HTML tag causes trouble...

First things first, there is a _long_ thread about SSI and Xitami in the list
archives. You may find the answers to your question there.

Second, remember, 2.5b5 is a _beta_ release, with built-in SSI support. The
possibility of something not working is something you take the responsibility
for when you decide to try it.

Try running 2.4d7 or 2.4d9, the SSI support is included via a Perl script, but
it does work.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Nov 17 00:12:25 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (M.A.Born)
Date: Sat, 17 Nov 2001 01:12:25 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] xitami needs improvement
References: <LAW2-OE75ZxAoaIv8tb00000004@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <3BF5AB69.60607@student.tue.nl>

I'm using ssi with Xitami 2.5b5 on windows 2000, and it works fine here, 
without even installing the perl-stuff.

Some ideas:

Does the page testssi.ssi work on your machine? 
(http://localhost/testssi.ssi), if so, ssi is set up correct and working 
(ssi should be working by default).
If not, check whether it's enabled in your defaults.cfg, the correct 
settings are: (from the xitami.cfg file)

[Ssi]
     enabled=1
[Wsx]
     .shtm=xixssi
     .shtml=xixssi
     .ssi=xixssi

Is the path of the included file correct? Put the include in the same 
directory as blah.shtm, and use <!--#include
 > virtual="blah.htm"-->

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Nov 18 08:45:36 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Stanislav Karchebny)
Date: Sun, 18 Nov 2001 13:45:36 +0500
Subject: [Xitami] $PHP_SELF
Message-ID: <1633424203.20011118134536@vismech.ru>

Use The Source, xitami!

I was just... messing around with my scripts and found one thing about
$PHP_SELF. Indeed, I encountered the problem long ago and just
invented a fix in my header file and even forgot about it :))

here's the PHP-side fix:

// win32 localhost workaround  -- berkus 2001.08.02 01:26 YEKST
if( strstr($SCRIPT_NAME, "\\\\") )
{
   $PHP_SELF = substr($SERVER_URL,0,-1).str_replace("\\\\", "/", $SCRIPT_NAME);
}

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Nov 19 12:18:04 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Mon, 19 Nov 2001 13:18:04 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] exploite ?
References: <761.722T2435T12154679rachael_@gmx.net>
Message-ID: <3BF8F87C.7050808@freesbee.fr>

>
>
>
>Then how can something in the /upload dir suddenly become readable when
>the ftpdirs.aut read:
>
>[pub/upload]                                                                    
>Anonymous=PM
>
>the problems aint that someone uploades something but that the /upload dirs
>suddenly becomes readable for an anonymous user, seeems as xitami dont 
>check the access rights in ftpdirs.aut as it should.
>
Well if yout have ftproot/pub for anonymous and
ftproot/upload for upload (two separate directories with no links 
between them) then the problem goes away.

This isn't a bug it a feature (sort of). Basically Xitami inherits 
permissions from the parent specified and by means of the method of access.

In your case you appear to have defined pub/ as G and pub/upload/ as PM. 
Unfortunately this means that because you can get to pub/upload from pub 
the permissions from pub also apply to pub/upload.


Francis

  experience is what you get when you don't." Pete Seeger

In-Reply-To: <20011120021447.97083.qmail@web12504.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20011120122551.91053.qmail@web14906.mail.yahoo.com>

I had this problem as well.  Same thing on windows XP.  I'll be d:\ is the
drive that Xitami is installed on, right?  For some reason it can't see
the root of the drive it's installed on.  What I did was share the drive,
map it to a new drive letter (x:\), and set the path /d to point to the
mapped drive x:\.  So, essentially you're still seeing drive d:\.  It
works for me.  Hope it helps.

SHANE

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Nov 20 14:14:42 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Tue, 20 Nov 2001 15:14:42 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Folder access Probs with 2000
References: <20011120122551.91053.qmail@web14906.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <3BFA6552.7040501@freesbee.fr>

Shane Smith wrote:

>I had this problem as well.  Same thing on windows XP.  I'll be d:\ is the
>drive that Xitami is installed on, right?  For some reason it can't see
>the root of the drive it's installed on.  What I did was share the drive,
>map it to a new drive letter (x:\), and set the path /d to point to the
>mapped drive x:\.  So, essentially you're still seeing drive d:\.  It
>works for me.  Hope it helps.
>
BIG BIG SECURITY HOLE HERE IF YOU AREN'T CAREFUL

Are you SURE you want to do this?

If you set aliasses like
     DDD = "d:/"
where D: is the drive that Xitami is instaleld on then you are asking 
someone to look at http://hostname/DDD/Xitami/defaults.cfg and 
http://hostname/DDD/Xitami/defaults.aut which means that you will show 
the world your configuration settings. If you've been really sloppy and 
allowed FTP to see http aliases then someone could put a trojan in place 
of your webserver by doing put ftp://hostname/DDD/Xitami/Xiwin32.exe 
trojan.exe

I don't want to be alarmist here but what Xitami is doing here is makign 
sure that you don't accidentally open up a huge security hole. This is 
GOOD and you really need to think about whether you actually want that 
hole to exist before trying to work around it!

BTW if Xitami is in C:\xitami and you share d:\ where d:\ is where you 
installed Win2k/XP thats still not the smartest thing to do since that 
allows people to see d:\winnt which has a lot of interesting information 
in it and again the potential for someone to upload a trojan exists.

Francis

-- 
"Education is when you read the fine print; 
  experience is what you get when you don't." Pete Seeger

i dont know weather or not this is the same problem but i have been using
cuteftp1.8 for a few years now and it has worked quite hapily.

i saw no problem when i moved from nt to 2000.

however a few months back i statted seeing only some or none of the dirs on
a drive or in a folder.

after much checking of  settings etc i discovered that simply upgrading to a
newer version of cuteftp fixed the problem.

Other than that you may have chosen "change to ntfs" when you were
installing 2000 and find yourself with one drive having a fat partition and
one drive being protected by the ntfs protection where permissions are
required.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Nov 21 09:41:28 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Angus Lord)

Subject: [Xitami] GSL with post variables
References: <07e701c1726e$b0bc1610$ee02a8c0@development.europeonline.net>
Message-ID: <07fc01c17270$b1882dc0$ee02a8c0@development.europeonline.net>

Sorry, found out how to do it myself. GSLgen inherits the cgi environment,
so all the variables passed to the script are in the environment variables
FORM_xxx (xxx being the name of the variable), and these can just be used
'as is'.

Need to make sure I've got enough environment space for it all now....

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Nov 21 15:51:21 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Wed, 21 Nov 2001 16:51:21 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] GSL &(symbol); expansion feature
Message-ID: <3BFBCD79.6040102@freesbee.fr>

This is more of an FYI than a bug report or question...

I can't see this documented but some experiemntation and subsequent 
source code examination (smt/formio.c - put_textual() line 850 ish) 
shows that Xitami/GSLgen will replace &(symbol); with the actual symbol 
during its symbol expansion if symbol is gt , lt , amp or quot. So any 
xml file with &gt; , &lt; , &amp; or &quot; will ouptut <>&" into stdout 
(or wherevere the output is).

Thus if you have a tag
<From>
Francis Turner &lt;francis.turner@freesbee.fr>
</From>

and the script has a line
From: <a href="mailto:$(->From:)">$(->From:)</a>

the output text is
From: <a href="mailto:Francis Turner 
<francis.turner@freesbee.fr>">Francis Turner 
<francis.turner@freesbee.fr></a>

and not as I would have expected
From: <a href="mailto:Francis Turner 
&lt;francis.turner@freesbee.fr>">Francis Turner 
&lt;francis.turner@freesbee.fr></a>

This is good because you can embed html tags within your XML files e.g.
<Contents>
a line of text with a &lt;href='/'>link to the top&lt;/a> in an XML tag
</Contents>

but leads to some interesting required gymnastics if you want to put the 
sequence &(symbol); on the page yourself to keep the users browser 
happy. Going back to the earlier From tag example - if you want to display
Francis Turner &lt;francis.turner@freesbee.fr>
so that the users browser actually displays the email address the tag 
contents needs to be
<From>
Francis Turner &amp;lt;francis.turner@freesbee.fr>
</From>

Share and Enjoy

Francis

-- 
"Education is when you read the fine print; 
  experience is what you get when you don't." Pete Seeger

server. Managing these have become cumbersome and creating new ones are not
much
easier ( I often have to directly edit the defaults.cfg file). Also if you
want to
allow people to manage they're own domains/subdomains as well as do checks
on
billing and what not then it becomes equally difficult since xitami doesn't
support
these features.

1) A list of specific functions and/or features that the system must support
2) Any graphical or user interface ideas

and re-write the entire file from the database. However, this would mean that
you could not use the Xitami admin html screen to modify the settings.

Subject: [Xitami] File locking problems

I am creating a dynamic web system where html (and xml) files are 
generated by perl cgi scripts and they are displayed using Xitami as 
static objects once  created.

Unfortunatley I think I've found a race condition, which causes Xitami 
to crash. The condition occurs when a static XML file includes a second 
file (using .xml from XXX or .literal from XXX) and the second file gets 
deleted or renamed just as its being read.

The problem is I don't know how I can lock a file in order to delete it 
(or rename it).

This doesn't happen very often and its very hard to make occur 
frequently so this is speculation, but I can't think what else is 
causing these occasional crashes. I'm wondering if it is something to do 
with the fatc that the perl script that does the deletion is running as 
a child of Xitami because it is called by CGI. Indeed it could be that 
the problem is that the CGI script is inable to delete/rename the file 
but I don't think so since I check the return codes - also the crash 
reports from Xitami and mention xixxml .... (though I did get one crash 
which just produced a dialog saying Microsoft Visual C++ has encountered 
an unrecoverable error with no log)

The system is win2000 sp1 + many security fixes

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Nov 26 09:30:15 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (bernd hohmann)
Date: Mon, 26 Nov 2001 10:30:15 +0100 (MEZ)
Subject: [Xitami] Looking for anyone interested in advancing Xitami
In-Reply-To: <002201c1745b$8d0697b0$c86dfc3e@home>
Message-ID: <200111260930.KAA31843@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

On Fri, 23 Nov 2001 20:15:08 -0000, Ben Sadler wrote:

> how did you get sub-domains to work on xitami? next year i want to move my
> domain to my computer, so that nameservers are running on my computer (its
> cheaper) and i would like to know how to do this.

as any other subdomain too: you define the subdomain in your DNS (like os2.harddiskcafe.de, www.harddiskcafe.de, ftp.harddiskafe.de) and create an entry in the [Virtual-Hosts] section of the xitami configuration.

os2.harddiskcafe.de=c:\www\vhosts\os2.harddiskcafe.de\vhost.cfg

in this vhost.cfg you define the differences in the configuration:

[Server]
    ipaddress=62.159.157.34
    webpages=c:\www\vhosts\os2.harddiskcafe.de\htdocs\
[AccessLog]
    filename=c:\www\vhosts\os2.harddiskcafe.de\logdata\access.log
   cycle-arg=c:\www\vhosts\os2.harddiskcafe.de\logdata\ac%yy%mm%dd.log
[ErrorLog]
    filename=c:\www\vhosts\os2.harddiskcafe.de\logdata\access.log
   cycle-arg=c:\www\vhosts\os2.harddiskcafe.de\logdata\ac%yy%mm%dd.log
[Security]
    filename=c:\www\vhosts\os2.harddiskcafe.de\vhost.aut
    dirlist=1

bernd

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Nov 29 04:11:49 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Bernd Luevelsmeyer)
Date: Thu, 29 Nov 2001 05:11:49 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] password in clear text
Message-ID: <20011129041149.C2EC4B8101@christel.heitec.net>

Hi,

on the Bugtraq mailing list, "Larry W. Cashdollar" raised the issue
of Xitami storing the admin password in clear text in its default
installation. If you are interested, please dig the archives at
http://www.securityfocus.com. The Message ID is
<20011126145820.R78965-100000@vapid.dhs.org> and the exact subject
is "Xitami Webserver stores admin password in clear text.".

On FreeBSD the program won't run automatically after installation,
but I'll provide more configuration help and safer defaults anyway.

Greetings,
	Bernd

<20011126145820.R78965-100000@vapid.dhs.org> and the exact subject
is "Xitami Webserver stores admin password in clear text.".

On FreeBSD the program won't run automatically after installation,
but I'll provide more configuration help and safer defaults anyway.

Greetings,
	Bernd

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Nov 29 11:24:34 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 30 Nov 2001 00:24:34 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] password in clear text
In-Reply-To: Message from Bernd Luevelsmeyer <bdluevel@heitec.net>
 of "Thu, 29 Nov 2001 05:11:49 BST." <20011129041149.C2EC4B8101@christel.heitec.net>
Message-ID: <200111291124.AAA16552@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <20011129041149.C2EC4B8101@christel.heitec.net>, Bernd Luevelsmeyer w
rites:
>on the Bugtraq mailing list, "Larry W. Cashdollar" raised the issue
>of Xitami storing the admin password in clear text in its default
>installation. 

While it is an issue (and has been in the FAQ for quite a while), the
situation that was discussed on Bugtraq (leading to a local root
exploit) requires:
- the plain text password file
- insecure permissions on the plain text password file
- an untrusted user with local access (web admin is local only by default)
- the webserver to be run as root

Having a plain text password in the file isn't ideal, but the combination
of untrusted local users, not checking the permissions on the file
containing the password, and running the server as root definitely don't
help either.

Xitami can be run as a non-root user (with a slight decrease in
functionality, or with the assistance of port redirection in the OS);
either started as root and have Xitami change to a non-root user (the
setuid functionality; but then the "restart" features in Xitami won't
work), or run on an off-numbered port (ie not port 80).  (If the OS
supports port redirection you can redirect port 80 to another one that
a normal user can bind to, and run Xitami on that port.)

The most direct step if you can't trust your local users is to change
the permissions on the password file to 0400 or 0600 (with the owner
being the user that runs Xitami), or to disable the web-based admin.
I typically do both on systems where I'm particularly concerned about
security.

>On FreeBSD the program won't run automatically after installation,
>but I'll provide more configuration help and safer defaults anyway.

Thanks for this, and thanks for your post to Bugtraq.  I do plan to
make my own post to Bugtraq -- but I'm still busy trying to catch
up with everything that needs to be done this week.  (And this issue
while obviously important, has a number of obvious workarounds, so is
less urgent than some of the security issues with other (non-iMatix)
products I've been dealing with today.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Hi Folks,

Well it appears that the Xitami mailing list got rather upset at someone
mentioning there was a problem with Xitami, and decided to retailiate :-)
(For those that missed out, it started sending out copy after copy after
copy after... of the same message Bernd Luevelsmeyer <bdluevel@heitec.net>
conerning a post to the Bugtraq mailing list about Xitami.)

Seriously, it appears that the mailing list software that we're using
and the iMatix mail server had a violent disagrement about the meaning
of a error message, which led the mailing list software to keep resending
the same message over and over again, even though the mail server
already had plenty of copies of the message which it was going to send
out real soon now and was just trying to say it wasn't going to be able
to send it immediately.

I _think_ I've found the original cause of the problem and put something
in place to stop it happening again, but I'm not sure why it would have
caused the behaviour to happen so unfortunately I'm not 100% certain
I've fixed the problem yet.

My apologies to everyone who got 5, 15, 30, or more copies of the same
message in their mailbox from the Xitami list.  I stopped as many as I
could (there were up to 100 more waiting to be sent out), but I've
received about 30 of them, and I think a few others got more.
