From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Nov 29 15:52:00 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Bernd Luevelsmeyer)
Date: Thu, 29 Nov 2001 16:52:00 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] password in clear text
References: <20011129041149.C2EC4B8101@christel.heitec.net> <3C061FB4.5010000@freesbee.fr> <20011129122022.03C0DB8101@christel.heitec.net> <3C06322F.9080505@freesbee.fr>
Message-ID: <20011129155200.427CEB8206@christel.heitec.net>

Francis Turner wrote:
[...]
> I think your point though is excellent. I would like to see Xitami do
> something like a MD5 hash on the password field. An alternative which
> would suit me just fine would be for the authetication to be handed of
> to the OS...

Handing it off to the OS would be most helpful for the FTP part,
where user really do log in. Xitami also should impersonate the user
then, so the OS will check file accesses automatically.
This is not easy, though, firstly there may be several user logged
in but you can only impersonate one of them, and secondly this is
highly OS specific but Xitami ought to be portable. For this reason,
I don't recommend using the FTP part at all on FreeBSD, but instead
use the server that comes with the OS anyway.

If Xitami runs as a specific user, and only that user has read
permission on the file, then the clear-text things are no problem
IMHO. Just make sure Xitami as a web browser of FTP server or CGI
owner can't be tricked to deliver the file to clients. The problem
is, per default the file is world-readable and Xitami runs as root.

On FreeBSD I made Xitami to install unconfigured and it won't start
automatically. So I left the issue for the admin to clean up: invent
a xitami-user, write defaults.cfg and defaults.aut, provide file
permissions, and set up the autostart-at-boot thingy. It's perhaps
not fair, but technically nobody is in any danger by this install
routine. I've not made up my mind exactly how to change it, but will
somehow do a more complete automatic install; perhaps let it run as
user "nobody" and provide a very restrictive defaults.cfg (only HTTP
and no remote administration).

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Nov 29 17:40:46 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Bob Paddock)
Date: Thu, 29 Nov 2001 12:40:46 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] lrwp php?
Message-ID: <200111291240187.SM00191@BOB-PADDOCK>

I've written a crude data base in PHP, it is doing what I need, but I was wondering if there was a way to turn a php program into a lrwp program?

The php program searches through some large text files, I'd like to have the text files loaded in memory so they don't keep being read from disk during each query.



From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Nov 29 18:11:47 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Thu, 29 Nov 2001 13:11:47 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] lrwp php?
References: <200111291240187.SM00191@BOB-PADDOCK>
Message-ID: <3C067A63.68CB7CFD@rci.rutgers.edu>

> searches through some large text files, I'd like to have the text files loaded in memory so they don't keep being read from disk during each query.

How large? Are you sure they are actually being read from disk? 

In unix and Windows, most available memory is used as disk cache. If you
have enough RAM to avoid thrashing, the second third etc time you read a
file that hasn't changed on disk, it usually comes from cache rather
than from physical disk.

You could test this by adding code to grab the time when the program
starts and is done, compute the difference, and write that at the bottom
of the search report. If I'm right, the very first time each day (or
re-boot, or RAM-overload) that it runs will be seconds, each subsequent
search will be milliseconds.

You might also grab the time before and after the file read and before
and after the search process, if they are two phases. In VB, a
case-sensitive search turned out to be FAR slower than any disk-work. 

I'm also sure that for VB and Perl, the interpreter start-up takes
longer than about any code I can write in a month. 

LRWP is a good idea, but hard to get working. Be sure you need the speed
and that it will really help before you go to that extreme. Many massive
sites work fine with plain CGI. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Nov 29 22:39:15 2001

Assuming y0u have one IP address for the server.

Set up Xitami or IIS to use a different port than the default of 80.
The to connect to that server you'd use this url:

http://<name or IP of your server:<port of server>
In my case I'm doing just that until I get my site moved off of ASP and onto PHP.  I run Xitami on port 8080 so I connect to it like this:  http://63.146.67.100:8080

Bob,

If you look through the code in the php 'sapi' (Server API) directory you will
find the code to build a fastcgi version of php. Given that lrwp is simpler than
fascgi and that Xitami provide an easy to use lrwp libray it should be a fairly
simple task to impliment an lrwp version of php.

Good luck !

Paul

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Nov 29 23:20:46 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul N Shortis)
Date: Fri, 30 Nov 2001 09:20:46 +1000
Subject: [Xitami] Issues/questions with 2.5b5
Message-ID: <4A256B13.0080493D.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>


Scott,

The 'php returns a blank page' comment is a dead give away - this is usually
because php.exe loads but is unable to load php4ts.dll. The most common solution
is to put php.exe and php4ts.dll into the xitami directory. This appears however
to be problematic with aliases. The solution for my problem was to place an
entry in the  system path that points to the php directory instead of moving the
php exe and dll. I also experimented with placing the dll in the winnt\system32
directory.

I think this will solve your questions 1 & 2.

If you wish to run Xitami with a particular account. Install Xitami as a
service. Then open the services control applet and open the service editor and
set the account name and password to run the service - this is standard windows
NT/2000 stuff.

Best of luck

Paul

On 29 Nov 2001 at 15:06, Cory Nelson wrote:

> OK, i'm trying to run a virtual host so that i can run two webpages off of
> one IP.  I can't find out how though.
> 
> Can somebody explain exactly how to set up a vhost, and if it requires
> running off of two ports, how do i specify which ports?
Are you trying to host 2 domains or two sub sites like this: www.yourdomain.com/siteA and www.yourdomain.com/siteB
To host domians you would use the Virtual Host configurations and setup a DNS based virtual host (vs an IP based) in the admin browser. To create the two subsites 
you would use the aliases configurations in the admin browser.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Nov 30 03:15:10 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)
Date: Thu, 29 Nov 2001 22:15:10 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] How do i run a virtual host?
References: <000201c1794a$0ebc8060$0502a8c0@amd900>
Message-ID: <3C06F9BE.73555AC3@2cah.com>

Jeff Toycen wrote:
> 
> Id like to hear about them as well as I had little success myself ..
> 
> -----Original Message-----
> Subject: [Xitami] How do i run a virtual host?
> 
> OK, i'm trying to run a virtual host so that i can run two webpages off
> of
> one IP.  I can't find out how though.

The short version. :-)

If you want to run two or more virtual-hosts off of a single IP address you
are going to have to use name based v-hosts. It is really a lot more simple
than it seems.

The first thing you need to do is create a configuration file for each v-host.
The easiest way to think about the configuration for each v-host is that the
configuration file is a defaults.cfg for _each_ host. Then in your
defaults.cfg you put a pointer/reference for the v-host configuration to that
file.

I'm going to use one.domain.com and two.domain.com in this example. The
_bare_minimum_ CFG file for each v-host is below:

---one.domain.com.cfg--start--
#*END

[Server]
    Defaults=defaults.cfg
    Webpages=one
    Hostname=one.domain.com
---one.domain.com.cfg--end--

---two.domain.com.cfg--start--
#*END

[Server]
    Defaults=defaults.cfg
    Webpages=two
    Hostname=two.domain.com
---two.domain.com.cfg--end--

Then in your defaults.cfg you'll need to add the [Virtual-hosts] section (note
the spacing at the beginning of each line):

--
[Virtual-hosts]
    One.domain.com=one.domain.com.cfg
    Two.domain.com=two.domain.com.cfg
--

The web files for one.domain.com would go in \xitami\webpages\one and for
two.domain.com in \xitami\webpages\two.

You'll also want to look into creating a basehost.cfg, which can be found in
the documentation here:

  http://localhost/xitami/index8.htm

Good luck! I hope this helps.

Xitami excels at name based virtual hosting. I'm running over 25 (at last
count) here with _zero_ problems what so ever.

-- 

Craig Morrison
  MTS Professional @ http://www.mtsprofessional.com/
  A Win32 Email server that works for _you_.

The manual tells you all about it
---------------------------------
using the webinterface makes this entries in your defaults.cfg
[Virtual-hosts]
    skynetsyndicate.dnsq.org=skynetsyndicate.cfg
    noaccess.dnsq.org=noaccess.cfg
    weird1.org=weird1.cfg

But to make this to work you need an dns server to resolve the headers...
Good tips and deeply how to  do it you find in the Xitami Faq
